<p>The <b>Shanghai Metro</b> is a <a href="/wiki/Rapid_transit" title="Rapid transit">rapid transit</a> system in <a href="/wiki/Shanghai" title="Shanghai">Shanghai</a>, China, operating urban and suburban rail transit services to 13 of its 16 <a href="/wiki/List_of_township-level_divisions_of_Shanghai" title="List of township-level divisions of Shanghai">municipal districts</a> (except <a href="/wiki/Fengxian_District" title="Fengxian District">Fengxian</a>, <a href="/wiki/Jinshan_District" title="Jinshan District">Jinshan</a> and <a href="/wiki/Chongming_District" title="Chongming District">Chongming</a>) and to Huaqiao Town, <a href="/wiki/Kunshan" title="Kunshan">Kunshan</a>, <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Jiangsu_Province" title="Jiangsu Province">Jiangsu Province</a>. Opening in 1993 with full-scale construction extending back to 1986, Shanghai Metro is the third oldest rapid transit system in <a href="/wiki/China" title="China">China</a>, after the <a href="/wiki/Beijing_Subway" title="Beijing Subway">Beijing Subway</a> and the <a href="/wiki/Tianjin_Metro" title="Tianjin Metro">Tianjin Metro</a>. It has seen substantial growth, significantly during the years leading up to the <a href="/wiki/Expo_2010" title="Expo 2010">2010 Shanghai World Expo</a>, and is still expanding, with its most recent expansions having opened in December 2015<sup class="plainlinks noprint asof-tag update" style="display:none;"><a class="external text" href="//en.wikipedia.org/w/index.php?title=Shanghai_Metro&amp;action=edit">[update]</a></sup>. It is the largest component of the Shanghai metropolitan rail transit network, together with the <a href="/wiki/Shanghai_Maglev_Train" title="Shanghai Maglev Train">Shanghai Maglev Train</a>, the <a href="/wiki/Zhangjiang_Tram" title="Zhangjiang Tram">Zhangjiang Tram</a> and the <a href="/wiki/China_Railway" title="China Railway">China Railway</a>-operated commuter rail services to <a href="/wiki/Jinshan_Railway" title="Jinshan Railway">Jinshan</a> and to <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Lingang_New_City" title="Lingang New City">Lingang New City</a> in <a href="/wiki/Pudong" title="Pudong">Pudong</a>. The metro system is also heavily tied with other forms of <a href="/wiki/Public_transport_in_Shanghai" title="Public transport in Shanghai">public transport in Shanghai</a>.</p>
<p>Currently, the Shanghai Metro system is the world's <a href="/wiki/List_of_metro_systems" title="List of metro systems">largest rapid transit system by route length</a><sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-6"><a href="#cite_note-6">[4]</a></sup><sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-UITP-figs_7-0"><a href="#cite_note-UITP-figs-7">[5]</a></sup><sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-8"><a href="#cite_note-8">[6]</a></sup><sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-longest_9-0"><a href="#cite_note-longest-9">[7]</a></sup><sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-BBC_10-0"><a href="#cite_note-BBC-10">[8]</a></sup> and <a href="/wiki/List_of_metro_systems" title="List of metro systems">second largest by number of stations</a><sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-Stncount_2-1"><a href="#cite_note-Stncount-2">[note 2]</a></sup> with 14 lines<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-exclude-maglev-22_1-2"><a href="#cite_note-exclude-maglev-22-1">[note 1]</a></sup> and <a href="/wiki/List_of_Shanghai_Metro_stations" title="List of Shanghai Metro stations">364 stations</a> totaling 588 kilometres (365 mi).<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-Shanghai-Line13.2C16_11-0"><a href="#cite_note-Shanghai-Line13.2C16-11">[9]</a></sup><sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-exclude-maglev-22_1-3"><a href="#cite_note-exclude-maglev-22-1">[note 1]</a></sup> It also ranks <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Metro_systems_by_annual_passenger_rides" title="Metro systems by annual passenger rides">second in the world by annual ridership</a> after the <a href="/wiki/Beijing_Subway" title="Beijing Subway">Beijing Subway</a>, with 3.068 billion rides delivered in 2015.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-ridership_3-2"><a href="#cite_note-ridership-3">[1]</a></sup> The daily ridership record was set at 11.7 million on December 31, 2016,<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-ridership_record_4-1"><a href="#cite_note-ridership_record-4">[2]</a></sup> while over 10 million people use the system on an average workday.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-12"><a href="#cite_note-12">[10]</a></sup></p>
<p>On 16 October 2013, with the extension of Line 11 into <a href="/wiki/Kunshan" title="Kunshan">Kunshan</a>, <a href="/wiki/Jiangsu" title="Jiangsu">Jiangsu</a> province, Shanghai Metro became the first rapid transit system in China to provide cross-provincial service and the second intercity metro after the <a href="/wiki/Guangfo_Metro" title="Guangfo Metro">Guangfo Metro</a>. Further plans to connect the Shanghai Metro with the metro systems of <a href="/wiki/Suzhou_Rail_Transit" title="Suzhou Rail Transit">Suzhou</a> and <a href="/wiki/Wuxi_Metro" title="Wuxi Metro">Wuxi</a> are under active review.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-suzhouwuxi_13-0"><a href="#cite_note-suzhouwuxi-13">[11]</a></sup> The first line connecting Shanghai Metro Line 11 and Suzhou Metro Line 3 is projected to be completed in 2020.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-14"><a href="#cite_note-14">[12]</a></sup> Ambitious expansion plans call for 25 Lines with over 1,000 km of length by 2025.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-15"><a href="#cite_note-15">[13]</a></sup> By then, every location in the central area of Shanghai will be within 600 meters of a subway station.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-16"><a href="#cite_note-16">[14]</a></sup></p>
<p></p>

<h2><span class="mw-headline" id="History">History</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Shanghai_Metro&amp;action=edit&amp;section=1" title="Edit section: History">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h2>
<div class="thumb tright">
<div class="thumbinner" style="width:402px;"><a class="image" href="/wiki/File:SHM_evolution_mid.gif"><img alt="" class="thumbimage" data-file-height="438" data-file-width="500" height="350" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/9/9f/SHM_evolution_mid.gif/400px-SHM_evolution_mid.gif" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/9/9f/SHM_evolution_mid.gif 1.5x" width="400"/></a>
<div class="thumbcaption">
<div class="magnify"><a class="internal" href="/wiki/File:SHM_evolution_mid.gif" title="Enlarge"></a></div>
Evolution of the Shanghai Metro</div>
</div>
</div>
<ul>
<li>May 28, 1993 – Southern section of Line 1 (<a href="/wiki/Shanghai_South_Railway_Station_(Metro)" title="Shanghai South Railway Station (Metro)">New Longhua</a>/<a href="/wiki/Shanghai_South_Railway_Station_(Metro)" title="Shanghai South Railway Station (Metro)">Shanghai South Railway Station</a> – <a href="/wiki/Xujiahui_Station" title="Xujiahui Station">Xujiahui</a>) enters operation<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-firstline_17-0"><a href="#cite_note-firstline-17">[15]</a></sup><sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-.E4.B8.8A.E6.B5.B7.E5.B9.B4.E9.89.B41996_18-0"><a href="#cite_note-.E4.B8.8A.E6.B5.B7.E5.B9.B4.E9.89.B41996-18">[16]</a></sup> (4.4 km).</li>
<li>April 10, 1995 – Line 1 (<a href="/wiki/Jinjiang_Park_Station" title="Jinjiang Park Station">Jinjiang Park</a> – <a href="/wiki/Shanghai_Railway_Station_(Metro)" title="Shanghai Railway Station (Metro)">Shanghai Railway Station</a>; including initial section, which opened 1993) enters operation <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-firstline_17-1"><a href="#cite_note-firstline-17">[15]</a></sup><sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-.E4.B8.8A.E6.B5.B7.E5.B9.B4.E9.89.B41996_18-1"><a href="#cite_note-.E4.B8.8A.E6.B5.B7.E5.B9.B4.E9.89.B41996-18">[16]</a></sup> (16.1 km).</li>
<li>December 28, 1996 – Southern extension to Line 1 (<a href="/wiki/Xinzhuang_Station_(Shanghai_Metro)" title="Xinzhuang Station (Shanghai Metro)">Xinzhuang</a> – <a href="/wiki/Jinjiang_Park_Station" title="Jinjiang Park Station">Jinjiang Park</a>) enters operation (4.5 km).<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-.E4.B8.8A.E6.B5.B7.E5.B9.B4.E9.89.B41997.E5.8D.81.E5.9B.9B_19-0"><a href="#cite_note-.E4.B8.8A.E6.B5.B7.E5.B9.B4.E9.89.B41997.E5.8D.81.E5.9B.9B-19">[17]</a></sup><sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-.E4.B8.8A.E6.B5.B7.E5.B9.B4.E9.89.B41997.E5.9B.9B.E5.8D.81.E5.9B.9B_20-0"><a href="#cite_note-.E4.B8.8A.E6.B5.B7.E5.B9.B4.E9.89.B41997.E5.9B.9B.E5.8D.81.E5.9B.9B-20">[18]</a></sup></li>
<li>Sept 20, 1999 – Line 2 (<a href="/wiki/Zhongshan_Park_Station" title="Zhongshan Park Station">Zhongshan Park</a> – <a href="/wiki/Longyang_Road_Station" title="Longyang Road Station">Longyang Road</a>) enters operation (16.3 km).<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-.E4.B8.8A.E6.B5.B7.E5.B9.B4.E9.89.B42000.E5.8D.81.E5.9B.9B_21-0"><a href="#cite_note-.E4.B8.8A.E6.B5.B7.E5.B9.B4.E9.89.B42000.E5.8D.81.E5.9B.9B-21">[19]</a></sup><sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-.E4.B8.8A.E6.B5.B7.E5.B9.B4.E9.89.B42000.E4.BA.8C.E5.8D.81.E5.85.AD_22-0"><a href="#cite_note-.E4.B8.8A.E6.B5.B7.E5.B9.B4.E9.89.B42000.E4.BA.8C.E5.8D.81.E5.85.AD-22">[20]</a></sup><sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-firstline_17-2"><a href="#cite_note-firstline-17">[15]</a></sup></li>
<li>December 26, 2000 – The eastern extension to Line 2 (<a href="/wiki/Longyang_Road_Station" title="Longyang Road Station">Longyang Road</a> – <a href="/wiki/Zhangjiang_Hi-Tech_Park_Station" title="Zhangjiang Hi-Tech Park Station">Zhangjiang Hi-tech Park</a>) (2.8 km)<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-.E4.B8.8A.E6.B5.B7.E5.B9.B4.E9.89.B42001_23-0"><a href="#cite_note-.E4.B8.8A.E6.B5.B7.E5.B9.B4.E9.89.B42001-23">[21]</a></sup><sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-firstline_17-3"><a href="#cite_note-firstline-17">[15]</a></sup> and Line 3 (<a href="/wiki/Shanghai_South_Railway_Station_(Metro)" title="Shanghai South Railway Station (Metro)">Shanghai South Railway Station</a> – <a href="/wiki/Jiangwan_Town_Station" title="Jiangwan Town Station">Jiangwan Town</a>) (24.6 km)<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-firstline_17-4"><a href="#cite_note-firstline-17">[15]</a></sup><sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-.E4.B8.8A.E6.B5.B7.E5.B9.B4.E9.89.B42001_23-1"><a href="#cite_note-.E4.B8.8A.E6.B5.B7.E5.B9.B4.E9.89.B42001-23">[21]</a></sup> open.</li>
<li>November 25, 2003 – Line 5 (<a href="/wiki/Xinzhuang_Station_(Shanghai_Metro)" title="Xinzhuang Station (Shanghai Metro)">Xinzhuang</a> – <a href="/wiki/Minhang_District" title="Minhang District">Minhang</a>) enters operation (17.2 km).<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-.E4.B8.8A.E6.B5.B7.E5.B9.B4.E9.89.B42004_24-0"><a href="#cite_note-.E4.B8.8A.E6.B5.B7.E5.B9.B4.E9.89.B42004-24">[22]</a></sup></li>
<li>December 28, 2004 – Northern extension to Line 1 (<a href="/wiki/Shanghai_Railway_Station_(Metro)" title="Shanghai Railway Station (Metro)">Shanghai Railway Station</a> – <a href="/wiki/Gongfu_Xincun_Station" title="Gongfu Xincun Station">Gongfu Xincun</a>) enters operation (12.4 km).<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-.E4.B8.8A.E6.B5.B7.E5.B9.B4.E9.89.B42005_25-0"><a href="#cite_note-.E4.B8.8A.E6.B5.B7.E5.B9.B4.E9.89.B42005-25">[23]</a></sup></li>
<li>December 31, 2005 – Line 4 enters operation, except the section between <a href="/wiki/Lancun_Road_Station" title="Lancun Road Station">Lancun Roa</a>d and <a href="/wiki/Damuqiao_Road_Station" title="Damuqiao Road Station">Damuqiao Road</a> that was delayed due to a construction accident.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-.E4.B8.8A.E6.B5.B7.E5.B9.B4.E9.89.B42006_26-0"><a href="#cite_note-.E4.B8.8A.E6.B5.B7.E5.B9.B4.E9.89.B42006-26">[24]</a></sup></li>
<li>December 18, 2006 – Northern extension to Line 3 (<a href="/wiki/Jiangwan_Town_Station" title="Jiangwan Town Station">Jiangwan Town</a> – <a href="/wiki/North_Jiangyang_Road_Station" title="North Jiangyang Road Station">North Jiangyang Road</a>) enters operation (15.7 km).<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-.E4.B8.8A.E6.B5.B7.E5.B9.B4.E9.89.B42007_27-0"><a href="#cite_note-.E4.B8.8A.E6.B5.B7.E5.B9.B4.E9.89.B42007-27">[25]</a></sup><sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-firstline_17-5"><a href="#cite_note-firstline-17">[15]</a></sup></li>
<li>December 30, 2006 – Western extension to Line 2 (<a href="/wiki/Songhong_Road_Station" title="Songhong Road Station">Songhong Road</a> – <a href="/wiki/Zhongshan_Park_Station" title="Zhongshan Park Station">Zhongshan Park</a>) enters operation (6.15 km).<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-firstline_17-6"><a href="#cite_note-firstline-17">[15]</a></sup><sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-.E4.B8.8A.E6.B5.B7.E5.B9.B4.E9.89.B42007_27-1"><a href="#cite_note-.E4.B8.8A.E6.B5.B7.E5.B9.B4.E9.89.B42007-27">[25]</a></sup></li>
<li>December 29, 2007 – Five lines or sections enter operation on the same day:<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-28"><a href="#cite_note-28">[26]</a></sup>
<ul>
<li>Second northern extension to Line 1 (<a href="/wiki/Gongfu_Xincun_Station" title="Gongfu Xincun Station">Gongfu Xincun</a> – <a href="/wiki/Fujin_Road_Station" title="Fujin Road Station">Fujin Road</a>) (3.4 km)<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-.E4.B8.8A.E6.B5.B7.E5.B9.B4.E9.89.B42008_29-0"><a href="#cite_note-.E4.B8.8A.E6.B5.B7.E5.B9.B4.E9.89.B42008-29">[27]</a></sup></li>
<li>Delayed section of Line 4 (Lancun Road – Damuqiao Road), completing the loop.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-.E4.B8.8A.E6.B5.B7.E5.B9.B4.E9.89.B42008_29-1"><a href="#cite_note-.E4.B8.8A.E6.B5.B7.E5.B9.B4.E9.89.B42008-29">[27]</a></sup></li>
<li>Line 6 (Gangcheng Road – South Lingyan Road) (31.1 km)<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-.E4.B8.8A.E6.B5.B7.E5.B9.B4.E9.89.B42008_29-2"><a href="#cite_note-.E4.B8.8A.E6.B5.B7.E5.B9.B4.E9.89.B42008-29">[27]</a></sup></li>
<li>Line 8 (Shiguang Road – Yaohua Road)<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-.E4.B8.8A.E6.B5.B7.E5.B9.B4.E9.89.B42008_29-3"><a href="#cite_note-.E4.B8.8A.E6.B5.B7.E5.B9.B4.E9.89.B42008-29">[27]</a></sup></li>
<li>Line 9 (Songjiang New Town– Guilin Road)<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-.E4.B8.8A.E6.B5.B7.E5.B9.B4.E9.89.B42008_29-4"><a href="#cite_note-.E4.B8.8A.E6.B5.B7.E5.B9.B4.E9.89.B42008-29">[27]</a></sup></li>
</ul>
</li>
<li>December 28, 2008 – Line 9 is extended from Guilin Road to Yishan Road, connecting with the rest of the metro network.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-.E4.B8.8A.E6.B5.B7.E5.B9.B4.E9.89.B42009_30-0"><a href="#cite_note-.E4.B8.8A.E6.B5.B7.E5.B9.B4.E9.89.B42009-30">[28]</a></sup></li>
<li>July 5, 2009 – Southern extension to Line 8 (<a href="/wiki/Yaohua_Road_Station" title="Yaohua Road Station">Yaohua Road</a> – <a href="/wiki/Shendu_Highway_Station" title="Shendu Highway Station">Shendu Highway</a>) enters operation (14.4 km).<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-.E4.B8.8A.E6.B5.B7.E5.B9.B4.E9.89.B42010_31-0"><a href="#cite_note-.E4.B8.8A.E6.B5.B7.E5.B9.B4.E9.89.B42010-31">[29]</a></sup></li>
<li>December 5, 2009 – Line 7 (<a href="/wiki/Shanghai_University_Station" title="Shanghai University Station">Shanghai University</a> – <a href="/wiki/Huamu_Road_Station" title="Huamu Road Station">Huamu Road</a>) enters operation (34.4 km).<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-.E4.B8.8A.E6.B5.B7.E5.B9.B4.E9.89.B42010_31-1"><a href="#cite_note-.E4.B8.8A.E6.B5.B7.E5.B9.B4.E9.89.B42010-31">[29]</a></sup><sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-32"><a href="#cite_note-32">[30]</a></sup></li>
<li>December 31, 2009 – The downtown section of Line 9 (<a href="/wiki/Yishan_Road_Station" title="Yishan Road Station">Yishan Road</a> – <a href="/wiki/Century_Avenue_Station" title="Century Avenue Station">Century Avenue</a>) and<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-.E4.B8.8A.E6.B5.B7.E5.B9.B4.E9.89.B42010_31-2"><a href="#cite_note-.E4.B8.8A.E6.B5.B7.E5.B9.B4.E9.89.B42010-31">[29]</a></sup> the first section of Line 11 (<a href="/wiki/Jiangsu_Road_Station" title="Jiangsu Road Station">Jiangsu Road</a> – <a href="/wiki/North_Jiading_Station" title="North Jiading Station">North Jiading</a>)<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-.E4.B8.8A.E6.B5.B7.E5.B9.B4.E9.89.B42010_31-3"><a href="#cite_note-.E4.B8.8A.E6.B5.B7.E5.B9.B4.E9.89.B42010-31">[29]</a></sup> open.</li>
<li>February 24, 2010 – Short section of eastern extension of Line 2 (Longyang Road - Guanglan Road) enters operation. Zhangjiang Hi-tech Park station is rebuilt underground.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-.E4.B8.8A.E6.B5.B7.E5.B9.B4.E9.89.B42011_33-0"><a href="#cite_note-.E4.B8.8A.E6.B5.B7.E5.B9.B4.E9.89.B42011-33">[31]</a></sup></li>
<li>March 16, 2010 – Second western extension to Line 2 (Xujing East – Songhong Road) enters operation, connecting <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Hongqiao_Airport" title="Hongqiao Airport">Hongqiao Airport</a> to the metro system.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-firstline_17-7"><a href="#cite_note-firstline-17">[15]</a></sup><sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-.E4.B8.8A.E6.B5.B7.E5.B9.B4.E9.89.B42011_33-1"><a href="#cite_note-.E4.B8.8A.E6.B5.B7.E5.B9.B4.E9.89.B42011-33">[31]</a></sup></li>
<li>March 29, 2010 – Branch line of Line 11 (Jiading Xincheng- Anting) enters operation.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-34"><a href="#cite_note-34">[32]</a></sup></li>
<li>April 8, 2010 – Eastern extension to Line 2 (Guanglan Road – Pudong International Airport) enters operation, connecting the two airports.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-.E4.B8.8A.E6.B5.B7.E5.B9.B4.E9.89.B42011_33-2"><a href="#cite_note-.E4.B8.8A.E6.B5.B7.E5.B9.B4.E9.89.B42011-33">[31]</a></sup><sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-35"><a href="#cite_note-35">[33]</a></sup></li>
<li>April 10, 2010 – Line 10 (New Jiangwan City – Hangzhong Road) enters operation.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-.E4.B8.8A.E6.B5.B7.E5.B9.B4.E9.89.B42011_33-3"><a href="#cite_note-.E4.B8.8A.E6.B5.B7.E5.B9.B4.E9.89.B42011-33">[31]</a></sup> Shanghai Metro becomes the longest metro system in the world after 15 years of breakneck growth.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-zaobao_36-0"><a href="#cite_note-zaobao-36">[34]</a></sup></li>
<li>April 20, 2010 – Expo section of Line 13 (Madang Road – Shibo Avenue) enters temporary operation.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-37"><a href="#cite_note-37">[35]</a></sup><sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-38"><a href="#cite_note-38">[36]</a></sup></li>
<li>July 1, 2010 – with the opening of <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Hongqiao_Railway_Station" title="Hongqiao Railway Station">Hongqiao Railway Station</a>, its <a href="/wiki/Hongqiao_Railway_Station_(Shanghai_Metro)" title="Hongqiao Railway Station (Shanghai Metro)">metro station of the same name</a> on Line 2 enters operation.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-39"><a href="#cite_note-39">[37]</a></sup></li>
<li>November 2, 2010 – With the end of <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Shanghai_Expo" title="Shanghai Expo">Shanghai Expo</a>, Expo section of Line 13 suspends service, to be reopened when the rest of the line is completed.</li>
<li>November 30, 2010 – Section of Line 10 (Longxi Road – Hongqiao Railway Station) enters operation, connecting the two terminals of Hongqiao Airport.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-.E4.B8.8A.E6.B5.B7.E5.B9.B4.E9.89.B42011_33-4"><a href="#cite_note-.E4.B8.8A.E6.B5.B7.E5.B9.B4.E9.89.B42011-33">[31]</a></sup></li>
<li>December 28, 2010 – The 10-km long northern extension to Line 7 (Shanghai University – Meilan Lake) enters operation.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-.E4.B8.8A.E6.B5.B7.E5.B9.B4.E9.89.B42011_33-5"><a href="#cite_note-.E4.B8.8A.E6.B5.B7.E5.B9.B4.E9.89.B42011-33">[31]</a></sup></li>
<li>April 12, 2011 – Oriental Sports Center Station Opens<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-.E4.B8.8A.E6.B5.B7.E5.B9.B4.E9.89.B42012_40-0"><a href="#cite_note-.E4.B8.8A.E6.B5.B7.E5.B9.B4.E9.89.B42012-40">[38]</a></sup><sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-41"><a href="#cite_note-41">[39]</a></sup></li>
<li>April 26, 2011 – Line 11 <a href="/wiki/East_Changji_Road_Station" title="East Changji Road Station">East Changji Road Station</a> opens.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-.E4.B8.8A.E6.B5.B7.E5.B9.B4.E9.89.B42012_40-1"><a href="#cite_note-.E4.B8.8A.E6.B5.B7.E5.B9.B4.E9.89.B42012-40">[38]</a></sup></li>
<li>June 30, 2011 – <a href="/wiki/Panguang_Road_Station" title="Panguang Road Station">Panguang Road</a> and <a href="/wiki/Liuhang_Station" title="Liuhang Station">Liuhang</a> Stations on Line 7 open.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-.E4.B8.8A.E6.B5.B7.E5.B9.B4.E9.89.B42012_40-2"><a href="#cite_note-.E4.B8.8A.E6.B5.B7.E5.B9.B4.E9.89.B42012-40">[38]</a></sup></li>
<li>December 30, 2012 – The southern extension of Line 9 (Songjiang South Railway Station – Songjiang Xincheng) opens<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-shm2012-12_42-0"><a href="#cite_note-shm2012-12-42">[40]</a></sup> and the first phase of Line 13 (Jinyun Road – Jinshajiang Road) opens as well.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-shm2012-12_42-1"><a href="#cite_note-shm2012-12-42">[40]</a></sup></li>
<li>August 31, 2013 – The second phase of Line 11 (Jiangsu Road – Luoshan Road) enters operation.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-43"><a href="#cite_note-43">[41]</a></sup></li>
<li>October 16, 2013 – The 6-km long branch extension of Line 11 (Anting – Huaqiao) enters operation. Shanghai Metro is extended into <a href="/wiki/Jiangsu" title="Jiangsu">Jiangsu</a> province.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-line11_44-0"><a href="#cite_note-line11-44">[42]</a></sup></li>
<li>December 29, 2013 – The eastern section of Line 12 (Tiantong Road - Jinhai Road) and Line 16 (Luoshan Road - Dishui Lake) both enter operation.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-12.E5.8F.B7.E7.BA.BF16.E5.8F.B7.E7.BA.BF.E8.BD.BD.E5.AE.A2.E8.AF.95.E8.BF.90.E8.90.A5_45-0"><a href="#cite_note-12.E5.8F.B7.E7.BA.BF16.E5.8F.B7.E7.BA.BF.E8.BD.BD.E5.AE.A2.E8.AF.95.E8.BF.90.E8.90.A5-45">[43]</a></sup></li>
<li>May 10, 2014 – Line 12 Extension to <a href="/wiki/Qufu_Road_Station" title="Qufu Road Station">Qufu Road Station</a>.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-46"><a href="#cite_note-46">[44]</a></sup></li>
<li>December 28, 2014 – Extensions to Line 13 (Jinshajiang Road – Changshou Road) and Line 16 (Luoshan Road – Longyang Road) open <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-Shanghai-Line13.2C16_11-1"><a href="#cite_note-Shanghai-Line13.2C16-11">[9]</a></sup></li>
<li>December 19, 2015 – Extensions to Line 11 (Luoshan Road – Kangxin Highway), Line 12 (Qufu Road - Qixin Road), Line 13 (Changshou Road – Shibo Avenue) open.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-47"><a href="#cite_note-47">[45]</a></sup></li>
<li>April 26, 2016 – <a href="/wiki/Disney_Resort_Station" title="Disney Resort Station">Disney Resort Station</a> on Line 11 opens.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-48"><a href="#cite_note-48">[46]</a></sup></li>
</ul>
<h2><span class="mw-headline" id="Lines">Lines</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Shanghai_Metro&amp;action=edit&amp;section=2" title="Edit section: Lines">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h2>
<div class="hatnote" role="note">For the Maglev Train and the China Railway-operated service formerly denoted as Line 22, see <a href="/wiki/Shanghai_Maglev_Train" title="Shanghai Maglev Train">Shanghai Maglev Train</a> and <a href="/wiki/Jinshan_Railway" title="Jinshan Railway">Jinshan Railway</a>.</div>
<p>There are currently 14 lines in operation, with Lines and services are denoted numerically as well as by characteristic colors, which are used as a visual aid for better distinction on station signage and on the exterior of trains, in the form of a colored block or belt.</p>
<p>Unlike in other systems such as the <a href="/wiki/New_York_City_Subway" title="New York City Subway">New York City Subway</a>, most tracks in the Shanghai Metro system are served by a single service; thus "Line X" usually refers both to the physical line and its service. The only exception is the segment shared by Lines 3 and 4, between <a href="/wiki/Hongqiao_Road_Station" title="Hongqiao Road Station">Hongqiao Road Station</a> and <a href="/wiki/Baoshan_Road_Station" title="Baoshan Road Station">Baoshan Road Station</a>, where both services use the same tracks and platforms.</p>

<h2><span class="mw-headline" id="Services">Services</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Shanghai_Metro&amp;action=edit&amp;section=3" title="Edit section: Services">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h2>
<p>Unlike in other systems such as the <a href="/wiki/New_York_City_Subway" title="New York City Subway">New York City Subway</a>, most tracks in the Shanghai Metro system are served by a single service; thus "Line X" usually refers both to the physical line and its service. The only exception is the segment shared by Lines 3 and 4, between <a href="/wiki/Hongqiao_Road_Station" title="Hongqiao Road Station">Hongqiao Road Station</a> and <a href="/wiki/Baoshan_Road_Station" title="Baoshan Road Station">Baoshan Road Station</a>, where both services use the same tracks and platforms.</p>
<h3><span class="mw-headline" id="Partial_service_patterns">Partial service patterns</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Shanghai_Metro&amp;action=edit&amp;section=4" title="Edit section: Partial service patterns">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h3>
<p>Partial service patterns exist on Lines 1, 2, 3, 6, 7, 8, 9, 11 and 12.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-:0_49-1"><a href="#cite_note-:0-49">[47]</a></sup><sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-:1_51-1"><a href="#cite_note-:1-51">[49]</a></sup><sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-:2_52-1"><a href="#cite_note-:2-52">[50]</a></sup><sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-:3_55-1"><a href="#cite_note-:3-55">[53]</a></sup><sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-:4_56-1"><a href="#cite_note-:4-56">[54]</a></sup><sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-:5_57-1"><a href="#cite_note-:5-57">[55]</a></sup><sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-:6_58-1"><a href="#cite_note-:6-58">[56]</a></sup><sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-:7_60-1"><a href="#cite_note-:7-60">[58]</a></sup><sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-:8_61-1"><a href="#cite_note-:8-61">[59]</a></sup> Partial services serve only a (usually busier) sub-segment of the entire physical line. In addition, Line 2 has a piecewise service pattern whereby the suburban segment between <a href="/wiki/Guanglan_Road_Station" title="Guanglan Road Station">Guanglan Road Station</a> and <a href="/wiki/Pudong_International_Airport_Station" title="Pudong International Airport Station">Pudong International Airport Station</a> is served by a 4-car fleet separately. Passengers traveling across Guanglan Road on Line 2 must change trains across the platform at Guanglan Road.</p>
<p>Line 11, one of the two branch lines of the metro system, operates a different partial service pattern. Trains travelling to and from the branch line terminate at <a href="/wiki/Huaqiao_Station_(Shanghai_Metro)" title="Huaqiao Station (Shanghai Metro)">Huaqiao Station</a> and <a href="/wiki/Sanlin_Station" title="Sanlin Station">Sanlin</a> respectively. Hence, a passenger who wants to travel from the terminus of the branch to the eastern terminus of the line, at <a href="/wiki/Disney_Resort_Station" title="Disney Resort Station">Disney Resort</a> must change trains.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-:7_60-2"><a href="#cite_note-:7-60">[58]</a></sup></p>
<h4><span class="mw-headline" id="Line_16">Line 16</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Shanghai_Metro&amp;action=edit&amp;section=5" title="Edit section: Line 16">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h4>
<p>Line 16, unlike the rest of the system, is built with an express track and operates a rush-hour express service. The service was canceled in January 30, 2014, due to lack of available trains, but resumed on March 21, 2016.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-64"><a href="#cite_note-64">[62]</a></sup><sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-65"><a href="#cite_note-65">[63]</a></sup><sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-Line16_66-0"><a href="#cite_note-Line16-66">[64]</a></sup></p>
<h3><span class="mw-headline" id="Announcements">Announcements</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Shanghai_Metro&amp;action=edit&amp;section=6" title="Edit section: Announcements">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h3>
<p>All trains in the Shanghai Metro display destinations in Simplified Chinese and English, and make announcements in <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Standard_Mandarin" title="Standard Mandarin">Standard Mandarin</a>, English, and (on line 16 only) <a href="/wiki/Shanghainese" title="Shanghainese">Shanghainese</a> in order to indicate next stations, directions, and partial/full-length service patterns.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-sh.sina.com.cn_67-0"><a href="#cite_note-sh.sina.com.cn-67">[65]</a></sup></p>
<h2><span class="mw-headline" id="Stations">Stations</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Shanghai_Metro&amp;action=edit&amp;section=7" title="Edit section: Stations">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h2>

<h3><span class="mw-headline" id="Transfer_stations">Transfer stations</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Shanghai_Metro&amp;action=edit&amp;section=8" title="Edit section: Transfer stations">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h3>
<p>There are two types of transfer stations: physical transfer stations and transit-card only ones. In a physical transfer station, passengers can transfer between subway lines without exiting a fare zone. In a transit-card only transfer station, however, passengers have to exit and re-enter fare zones as they transfer from one subway line to another. In order to receive a discounted fare, passengers must use a <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Shanghai_public_transport_card" title="Shanghai public transport card">Shanghai public transport card</a> (SPTC) instead of Single-Ride tickets.</p>

<ul>
<li><a href="/wiki/Baoshan_Road_Station" title="Baoshan Road Station">Baoshan Road</a>, <a href="/wiki/Shanghai_Railway_Station_(Metro)" title="Shanghai Railway Station (Metro)">Shanghai Railway Station</a>, <a href="/wiki/Zhongtan_Road_Station" title="Zhongtan Road Station">Zhongtan Road</a>, <a href="/wiki/Zhenping_Road_Station" title="Zhenping Road Station">Zhenping Road</a>, <a href="/wiki/Caoyang_Road_Station" title="Caoyang Road Station">Caoyang Road</a>, <a href="/wiki/Jinshajiang_Road_Station" title="Jinshajiang Road Station">Jinshajiang Road</a>, <a href="/wiki/Zhongshan_Park_Station" title="Zhongshan Park Station">Zhongshan Park</a>, <a href="/wiki/West_Yan%27an_Road_Station" title="West Yan'an Road Station">West Yan'an Road</a> and <a href="/wiki/Hongqiao_Road_Station" title="Hongqiao Road Station">Hongqiao Road</a> are interchanges between Lines <b><a href="/wiki/Line_3,_Shanghai_Metro" title="Line 3, Shanghai Metro">3</a></b> and <b><a href="/wiki/Line_4,_Shanghai_Metro" title="Line 4, Shanghai Metro">4</a></b>. This is where the two lines share tracks between Baoshan Road and Hongqiao Road.</li>
<li>Lines 4 and 6 stop at two different stations both known as <a class="mw-redirect mw-disambig" href="/wiki/Pudian_Road_Station_(disambiguation)" title="Pudian Road Station (disambiguation)">Pudian Road</a>, but these two stations are not located together and interchanging is not possible.</li>
<li><a href="/wiki/Longyang_Road_Station" title="Longyang Road Station">Longyang Road</a> and <a href="/wiki/Pudong_International_Airport_Station" title="Pudong International Airport Station">Pudong International Airport</a> stations also provide transfers to the <a href="/wiki/Shanghai_Maglev_Train" title="Shanghai Maglev Train">Shanghai Maglev Train</a>, though passengers have to make another payment if they board the Maglev train.</li>
</ul>
<h4><span class="mw-headline" id="Transit-card_only_transfer_stations">Transit-card only transfer stations</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Shanghai_Metro&amp;action=edit&amp;section=9" title="Edit section: Transit-card only transfer stations">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h4>
<p>A transit-card only transfer station is a station where two lines meet, but unlike a physical interchange, there is no direct pathway between them within the paid fare area. Passengers wishing to interchange must exit the paid fare area for the first line, walk a short distance on the street, and re-enter the paid fare area for the second line. Since June 1, 2008, passengers interchanging using a <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Shanghai_public_transport_card" title="Shanghai public transport card">Shanghai public transport card</a> have their trip regarded as one journey and the distance will be accumulated for fare calculation. Passengers must exit a station and re-enter another within 30 minutes using the same Shanghai public transport card. Those using single-ride tickets cannot use virtual transfers and must purchase a new ticket.</p>
<p>In some cases virtual interchanges in place during a period of construction were superseded by physical interchanges at the completion of the construction. For example, <a href="/wiki/Hongkou_Football_Stadium_Station" title="Hongkou Football Stadium Station">Hongkou Football Stadium Station</a> was previously a virtual interchange between Line 3 and Line 8. Another previously virtual interchange was <a href="/wiki/South_Shaanxi_Road_Station" title="South Shaanxi Road Station">South Shaanxi Road Station</a> between <a href="/wiki/Line_1,_Shanghai_Metro" title="Line 1, Shanghai Metro">Line 1</a> and <a href="/wiki/Line_10,_Shanghai_Metro" title="Line 10, Shanghai Metro">Line 10</a>; after the opening of an extension of line 12 to the station in December 2015 transfers among all three lines became a physical interchange.</p>
<p>The current virtual interchanges are:</p>
<ul>
<li><a href="/wiki/Hongqiao_Airport_Terminal_2_Station" title="Hongqiao Airport Terminal 2 Station">Hongqiao Airport Terminal 2 Station</a> is a virtual interchange station between <b><a href="/wiki/Line_2,_Shanghai_Metro" title="Line 2, Shanghai Metro">Line 2</a></b> and <b><a href="/wiki/Line_10,_Shanghai_Metro" title="Line 10, Shanghai Metro">Line 10</a></b>.</li>
<li><a href="/wiki/Longhua_Station_(Shanghai_Metro)" title="Longhua Station (Shanghai Metro)">Longhua Station</a> is a virtual interchange station among <b><a href="/wiki/Line_11,_Shanghai_Metro" title="Line 11, Shanghai Metro">Line 11</a></b> and <b><a href="/wiki/Line_12,_Shanghai_Metro" title="Line 12, Shanghai Metro">Line 12</a></b>.</li>
<li><a href="/wiki/Shanghai_Railway_Station_(Metro)" title="Shanghai Railway Station (Metro)">Shanghai Railway Station</a> is a virtual interchange station between <b><a href="/wiki/Line_1,_Shanghai_Metro" title="Line 1, Shanghai Metro">Line 1</a></b> and <b><a href="/wiki/Line_3,_Shanghai_Metro" title="Line 3, Shanghai Metro">Line 3</a> / <a href="/wiki/Line_4,_Shanghai_Metro" title="Line 4, Shanghai Metro">Line 4</a></b>, but <a href="/wiki/Line_3,_Shanghai_Metro" title="Line 3, Shanghai Metro">Line 3</a> and <a href="/wiki/Line_4,_Shanghai_Metro" title="Line 4, Shanghai Metro">Line 4</a> share the same platforms and the transfer between Lines 3 and 4 can be made by simply waiting for the next train to arrive at the platform.</li>
<li><a href="/wiki/West_Nanjing_Road_Station" title="West Nanjing Road Station">West Nanjing Road Station</a> is a virtual interchange station among <b><a href="/wiki/Line_2,_Shanghai_Metro" title="Line 2, Shanghai Metro">Line 2</a></b>, <b><a href="/wiki/Line_12,_Shanghai_Metro" title="Line 12, Shanghai Metro">Line 12</a></b> and <b><a href="/wiki/Line_13,_Shanghai_Metro" title="Line 13, Shanghai Metro">Line 13</a></b>.</li>
</ul>
<h3><span class="mw-headline" id="Transport_hubs">Transport hubs</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Shanghai_Metro&amp;action=edit&amp;section=10" title="Edit section: Transport hubs">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h3>
<p>The busiest station in Shanghai Metro system is <a href="/wiki/People%27s_Square_Station" title="People's Square Station">People's Square</a> station (Lines <b><a href="/wiki/Line_1,_Shanghai_Metro" title="Line 1, Shanghai Metro">1</a></b>, <b><a href="/wiki/Line_2,_Shanghai_Metro" title="Line 2, Shanghai Metro">2</a></b> and <b><a href="/wiki/Line_8,_Shanghai_Metro" title="Line 8, Shanghai Metro">8</a></b>). As the interchange station for three lines, it is extremely crowded during peak hours. It remains busy during the rest of the day as it is located near major shopping and tourist destinations such as <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Nanjing_Road_(Shanghai)" title="Nanjing Road (Shanghai)">East Nanjing Road</a>, a pedestrian street, as well as the <a href="/wiki/Shanghai_Museum" title="Shanghai Museum">Shanghai Museum</a>, <a href="/wiki/People%27s_Park_(Shanghai)" title="People's Park (Shanghai)">People's Park</a>, the <a href="/wiki/Shanghai_Grand_Theatre" title="Shanghai Grand Theatre">Shanghai Grand Theatre</a> and Yan'an Park on <a href="/wiki/People%27s_Square" title="People's Square">People's Square</a>. It has the second largest number of exits (totalling 17) in the stations of the metro system.</p>
<p><a href="/wiki/Xujiahui_Station" title="Xujiahui Station">Xujiahui</a> (Lines <b><a href="/wiki/Line_1,_Shanghai_Metro" title="Line 1, Shanghai Metro">1</a></b>, <b><a href="/wiki/Line_9,_Shanghai_Metro" title="Line 9, Shanghai Metro">9</a></b> and <b><a href="/wiki/Line_11,_Shanghai_Metro" title="Line 11, Shanghai Metro">11</a></b>) is located in the major <a href="/wiki/Xujiahui" title="Xujiahui">Xujiahui</a> commercial center of Shanghai. Six large <a href="/wiki/Shopping_mall" title="Shopping mall">shopping malls</a> and eight large office towers are each within a three-minute walk of one of the station's exits, numbering a total of 18 since the addition of the four in the Line 9 part of the station that opened in December 2009. This is the largest number of exits of all the stations on the system. This station is also widely used as a pedestrian tunnel across the wide roads.</p>
<p><a href="/wiki/Lujiazui_Station" title="Lujiazui Station">Lujiazui</a> (Line <b><a href="/wiki/Line_2,_Shanghai_Metro" title="Line 2, Shanghai Metro">2</a></b>) is the major station in Pudong area. It is situated in the heart of Lujiazui financial district, the financial center of Shanghai. The city's iconic landmarks, the <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Oriental_Pearl_TV_Tower" title="Oriental Pearl TV Tower">Oriental Pearl TV Tower</a>, <a href="/wiki/Jin_Mao_Tower" title="Jin Mao Tower">Jin Mao Tower</a> and <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Shanghai_World_Financial_Centre" title="Shanghai World Financial Centre">Shanghai World Financial Centre</a> are all within walking distance of the station. In contrast to Xujiahui and People's Square, Lujiazui is not particularly busy during off-peak hours or on weekends as it is located in financial district of Shanghai.</p>
<p><a href="/wiki/Shanghai_Railway_Station_(Metro)" title="Shanghai Railway Station (Metro)">Shanghai Railway Station</a> (Lines <b><a href="/wiki/Line_1,_Shanghai_Metro" title="Line 1, Shanghai Metro">1</a></b>, <b><a href="/wiki/Line_3,_Shanghai_Metro" title="Line 3, Shanghai Metro">3</a></b> and <b><a href="/wiki/Line_4,_Shanghai_Metro" title="Line 4, Shanghai Metro">4</a></b>) is a major transportation hub in Shanghai, containing the railway station, two subway lines and the stop for many city bus lines as well as interprovincial buses. These bus lines will soon be housed in a brand-new bus station. The line 1 platform is in the South square while platforms for line 3/4 are in the North square. These two platforms are technically separate stations, so interchange is only possible between lines 3/4. A transfer to the line 1 platform requires a SPTC or a new ticket.</p>
<p><a href="/wiki/Shanghai_South_Railway_Station" title="Shanghai South Railway Station">Shanghai South Railway Station</a> (Lines <b><a href="/wiki/Line_1,_Shanghai_Metro" title="Line 1, Shanghai Metro">1</a></b> and <b><a href="/wiki/Line_3,_Shanghai_Metro" title="Line 3, Shanghai Metro">3</a></b>) is a transport station for line 1 and line 3; and the maintenance base of line 1 is also located at Shanghai South Railway Station.</p>
<p><a href="/wiki/Zhongshan_Park_Station" title="Zhongshan Park Station">Zhongshan Park Station</a> (Lines <b><a href="/wiki/Line_2,_Shanghai_Metro" title="Line 2, Shanghai Metro">2</a></b>, <b><a href="/wiki/Line_3,_Shanghai_Metro" title="Line 3, Shanghai Metro">3</a></b> and <b><a href="/wiki/Line_4,_Shanghai_Metro" title="Line 4, Shanghai Metro">4</a></b>) is a heavily trafficked station due to the large shopping malls and hotel immediately above it.</p>
<p><a href="/wiki/Century_Avenue_Station" title="Century Avenue Station">Century Avenue Station</a> (Lines <b><a href="/wiki/Line_2,_Shanghai_Metro" title="Line 2, Shanghai Metro">2</a></b>, <b><a href="/wiki/Line_4,_Shanghai_Metro" title="Line 4, Shanghai Metro">4</a></b>, <b><a href="/wiki/Line_6,_Shanghai_Metro" title="Line 6, Shanghai Metro">6</a></b> and <b><a href="/wiki/Line_9,_Shanghai_Metro" title="Line 9, Shanghai Metro">9</a></b>) is the largest interchange station in the Shanghai Metro system.</p>
<p><a href="/wiki/Pudong_International_Airport_Station" title="Pudong International Airport Station">Pudong International Airport</a> (Line <b><a href="/wiki/Line_2,_Shanghai_Metro" title="Line 2, Shanghai Metro">2</a></b>) is the eastern terminus of Line 2. It serves the <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Pudong_International_Airport" title="Pudong International Airport">airport of the same name</a> in Shanghai. The station also provides a transfer with the <a href="/wiki/Shanghai_Maglev_Train" title="Shanghai Maglev Train">Shanghai Maglev Train</a> to Longyang Road.</p>
<p><a href="/wiki/Hongqiao_Railway_Station_(Shanghai_Metro)" title="Hongqiao Railway Station (Shanghai Metro)">Hongqiao Railway Station</a> (Line <b><a href="/wiki/Line_2,_Shanghai_Metro" title="Line 2, Shanghai Metro">2</a></b> and Line <b><a href="/wiki/Line_10,_Shanghai_Metro" title="Line 10, Shanghai Metro">10</a></b>), <a href="/wiki/Hongqiao_Airport_Terminal_1_Station" title="Hongqiao Airport Terminal 1 Station">Hongqiao Airport Terminal 1</a> and <a href="/wiki/Hongqiao_Airport_Terminal_2_Station" title="Hongqiao Airport Terminal 2 Station">Hongqiao Airport Terminal 2</a> are metro stations located in the <a class="new" href="/w/index.php?title=Hongqiao_Comprehensive_Transportation_Hub&amp;action=edit&amp;redlink=1" title="Hongqiao Comprehensive Transportation Hub (page does not exist)">Hongqiao Comprehensive Transportation Hub</a>, composed of the <a href="/wiki/Shanghai_Hongqiao_International_Airport" title="Shanghai Hongqiao International Airport">Shanghai Hongqiao International Airport</a> and <a href="/wiki/Shanghai_Hongqiao_Railway_Station" title="Shanghai Hongqiao Railway Station">Shanghai Hongqiao Railway Station</a>. Both Hongqiao Airport stations are directly linked with the airport, offering many domestic and limited international flights, and the Hongqiao Railway metro station is directly linked with the train station. The airport and railway stations themselves offer a zero-distance transfer.</p>
<h2><span class="mw-headline" id="Ticket_system">Ticket system</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Shanghai_Metro&amp;action=edit&amp;section=11" title="Edit section: Ticket system">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h2>
<div class="thumb tright">
<div class="thumbinner" style="width:222px;"><a class="image" href="/wiki/File:Jiaotong_University_Station_Line_10_Platform.jpg"><img alt="" class="thumbimage" data-file-height="1200" data-file-width="1600" height="165" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/1/18/Jiaotong_University_Station_Line_10_Platform.jpg/220px-Jiaotong_University_Station_Line_10_Platform.jpg" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/1/18/Jiaotong_University_Station_Line_10_Platform.jpg/330px-Jiaotong_University_Station_Line_10_Platform.jpg 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/1/18/Jiaotong_University_Station_Line_10_Platform.jpg/440px-Jiaotong_University_Station_Line_10_Platform.jpg 2x" width="220"/></a>

</div>
</div>
<div class="thumb tright">
<div class="thumbinner" style="width:222px;"><a class="image" href="/wiki/File:Dabaishu_Station.jpg"><img alt="" class="thumbimage" data-file-height="768" data-file-width="1024" height="165" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/b/b4/Dabaishu_Station.jpg/220px-Dabaishu_Station.jpg" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/b/b4/Dabaishu_Station.jpg/330px-Dabaishu_Station.jpg 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/b/b4/Dabaishu_Station.jpg/440px-Dabaishu_Station.jpg 2x" width="220"/></a>

<div class="magnify"><a class="internal" href="/wiki/File:Dabaishu_Station.jpg" title="Enlarge"></a></div>
Dabaishu Station</div>
</div>
</div>
<p>Like many other metro systems in the world, Shanghai Metro uses a distance-based fare system.The system uses a "one-ticket network", which means that interchanging is possible between all interchange stations, given that the transfer staying within the Shanghai Metro system, without the purchase of another ticket where available. The <a href="/wiki/Shanghai_Public_Transport_Card" title="Shanghai Public Transport Card">Shanghai Public Transport Card</a>, which allows access to most public transport in Shanghai under one card, is another form of payment.</p>
<h3><span class="mw-headline" id="Fares">Fares</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Shanghai_Metro&amp;action=edit&amp;section=12" title="Edit section: Fares">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h3>
<ul>
<li>For most lines, the base fare is 3 <a href="/wiki/Chinese_yuan" title="Chinese yuan">yuan</a> for journeys under 6 km, then 1 yuan for each additional 10 km. As of December 2013, the highest fare is 14 yuan.</li>
<li>For journeys exclusively on <a href="/wiki/Line_5,_Shanghai_Metro" title="Line 5, Shanghai Metro">Line 5</a> (Xinzhuang – Minhang Development Zone), the fare is 2 yuan for journeys under 6 km and all other journeys are 3 yuan (though the total length of this line is a bit longer than 16 km).</li>
<li>Users of the <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Shanghai_public_transport_card" title="Shanghai public transport card">Shanghai public transport card</a> get a 10% discount for the rest of the calendar month after paying 70 yuan. The discount is applied only for journeys after the payment; it is not retroactively applied to previous journeys.</li>
<li>Users of the <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Shanghai_public_transport_card" title="Shanghai public transport card">Shanghai public transport card</a> as part of the "Air-conditioned Bus Transfer Discount" get a 1 yuan discount when transferring to the metro within 90 minutes. (The 10% monthly discount may be applied after the transfer discount) This discount also applies for bus to Metro and bus to bus transfers and can accumulate over multiple transfers. For example, to get from Zhenbei Rd/Meichuan Rd to Xiuyan Rd/Hunan Rd would normally cost 8 yuan each way (947 bus to line 4 to 451 bus) but only costs 6 RMB with the card (947 bus discounted transfer to line 4, discounted transfer to 451 bus). Depending on the time spent at the destination the discount will be applied at the start of the return trip as well, making the cost of a round-trip 11 yuan instead of the 16 yuan that would normally be charged without the card.</li>
</ul>
<h3><span class="mw-headline" id="Single_Journey_ticket">Single Journey ticket</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Shanghai_Metro&amp;action=edit&amp;section=13" title="Edit section: Single Journey ticket">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h3>
<p>Single-Journey tickets can be purchased from ticket vending machines, and at some stations, at a ticket window. Single-ride tickets are embedded with RFID contactless chips. When entering the system riders tap the ticket against a scanner above the turnstile, and on exit they insert the ticket into a slot where it is stored and recycled.</p>

<h3><span class="mw-headline" id="Shanghai_Public_Transportation_Card">Shanghai Public Transportation Card</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Shanghai_Metro&amp;action=edit&amp;section=14" title="Edit section: Shanghai Public Transportation Card">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h3>
<div class="hatnote" role="note">Main article: <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Shanghai_Public_Transportation_Card" title="Shanghai Public Transportation Card">Shanghai Public Transportation Card</a></div>
<p>In addition to a Single-Ride ticket, fare can be paid using a <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Shanghai_public_transport_card" title="Shanghai public transport card">Shanghai public transport card</a>. This RFID-embedded card can be purchased at selected banks, convenience stores and metro stations with a 20-yuan deposit. This card can be loaded at ticket booths, Service Centers at the metro stations as well as many small convenience stores and banks throughout the city. The Shanghai Public Transportation Card can also be used to pay for other forms of transportation, such as taxi or bus.</p>
<p>This transit card is similar to the <a href="/wiki/Oyster_card" title="Oyster card">Oyster card</a> of the <a href="/wiki/London_Underground" title="London Underground">London Underground</a> (and other London transport systems), <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Chicago_card" title="Chicago card">Chicago card</a> of the <a href="/wiki/Chicago_Transit_Authority" title="Chicago Transit Authority">CTA</a> and the <a href="/wiki/Octopus_card" title="Octopus card">Octopus card</a> of Hong Kong's <a href="/wiki/MTR" title="MTR">MTR</a>.</p>
<h3><span class="mw-headline" id="One-day_pass">One-day pass</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Shanghai_Metro&amp;action=edit&amp;section=15" title="Edit section: One-day pass">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h3>
<p>A one-day pass was introduced for the <a href="/wiki/Expo_2010" title="Expo 2010">Expo 2010</a> held in Shanghai. The fare for the calendar day was set at 18 <a href="/wiki/Chinese_yuan" title="Chinese yuan">yuan</a>, for unlimited travel within the metro system. This is not available through vending machines, but has to be purchased at Service Centers at metro stations.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-68"><a href="#cite_note-68">[66]</a></sup></p>
<h3><span class="mw-headline" id="Three-day_pass">Three-day pass</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Shanghai_Metro&amp;action=edit&amp;section=16" title="Edit section: Three-day pass">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h3>
<p>A three-day pass is available for Shanghai Metro. The fare for three days was set at 45 <a href="/wiki/Chinese_yuan" title="Chinese yuan">yuan</a>, for unlimited travel within the metro system. This is not available through vending machines, but has to be purchased at Service Centers at metro stations.</p>
<h2><span class="mw-headline" id="Infrastructure">Infrastructure</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Shanghai_Metro&amp;action=edit&amp;section=17" title="Edit section: Infrastructure">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h2>

<h3><span class="mw-headline" id="Gauge">Gauge</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Shanghai_Metro&amp;action=edit&amp;section=18" title="Edit section: Gauge">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h3>
<p><a href="/wiki/Standard_gauge" title="Standard gauge">Standard gauge</a> is used throughout the network, allowing new train equipment to be transported over the Chinese rail network which uses the same gauge.</p>
<h3><span class="mw-headline" id="Stations_2">Stations</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Shanghai_Metro&amp;action=edit&amp;section=19" title="Edit section: Stations">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h3>
<p>Almost all stations, except elevated sections and sections of Line 2, have <a href="/wiki/Platform_screen_doors" title="Platform screen doors">platform screen doors</a> with sliding <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Acrylic_glass" title="Acrylic glass">acrylic glass</a> at the platform edge. The train stops with its doors lined-up with the sliding doors on the platform edge and open when the train doors open, and are closed at other times. These screens are also being retrofitted on existing lines, starting with Line 1 whose core stations had doors by the end of 2006. On Line 2 and elevated sections (Line 3 and partly 4), the platform has sliding safety doors that reach only halfway up from the ground called <a href="/wiki/Automatic_platform_gate" title="Automatic platform gate">Automatic platform gates</a>. However, many of the sliding safety doors on the shared section of Line 3/4 only operate during peak times.</p>
<h3><span class="mw-headline" id="Rolling_stock">Rolling stock</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Shanghai_Metro&amp;action=edit&amp;section=20" title="Edit section: Rolling stock">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h3>
<table class="plainlinks metadata ambox ambox-content ambox-Unreferenced" role="presentation">
<tr>
<td class="mbox-image">

<td class="mbox-text"><span class="mbox-text-span">This section <b>does not <a href="/wiki/Wikipedia:Citing_sources" title="Wikipedia:Citing sources">cite</a> any <a href="/wiki/Wikipedia:Verifiability" title="Wikipedia:Verifiability">sources</a></b>. <span class="hide-when-compact">Please help <a class="external text" href="//en.wikipedia.org/w/index.php?title=Shanghai_Metro&amp;action=edit">improve this section</a> by <a href="/wiki/Help:Introduction_to_referencing_with_Wiki_Markup/1" title="Help:Introduction to referencing with Wiki Markup/1">adding citations to reliable sources</a>. </table>
<p>Train sets used by the Metro system:</p>
<ul>
<li>134 <a href="/wiki/Bombardier_Transportation" title="Bombardier Transportation">Bombardier</a> <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Movia" title="Movia">Movia</a> 456 six car sets(AC04) - Lines 9, 7 and 12</li>
<li>61 <a href="/wiki/German_Shanghai_Metro_Group" title="German Shanghai Metro Group">German Shanghai Metro Group</a> (GSMG) six cars units (Coded as AC01 for those using Alternating Current or DC01 for those using Direct Current for Line 1, AC02 for Line 2) – Line 1 and 2 (all reformed to eight car units)</li>
<li>53 Alstom Metropolis eight car sets(Coded as AC06) – Line 1, (Coded as AC08) – Line 2</li>
<li>16 Alstom Metropolis four car sets(AC06) - Section of Line 2</li>
<li>17 Alstom Metropolis four car sets - Line 5</li>
<li>21 Alstom Metropolis four car sets(AC06) - Line 6</li>
<li>28 Alstom Metropolis six car or seven car sets - Line 8</li>
<li>29 CNR <a href="/wiki/Changchun_Railway_Vehicles" title="Changchun Railway Vehicles">Changchun Railway Vehicles</a> Co., Ltd. four car sets - line 6</li>
<li>38 CNR <a href="/wiki/Changchun_Railway_Vehicles" title="Changchun Railway Vehicles">Changchun Railway Vehicles</a> Co., Ltd. seven car sets - line 8</li>
<li>28 <a href="/wiki/Alstom" title="Alstom">Alstom</a> <a href="/wiki/Alstom_Metropolis" title="Alstom Metropolis">Metropolis</a> six car sets(AC03) – Line 3</li>
<li>86 <a href="/wiki/Siemens" title="Siemens">Siemens</a> &amp; <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/CSR_Zhuzhou" title="CSR Zhuzhou">CSR Zhuzhou</a> six car sets(AC05) - Line 4 and 11</li>
<li>41 <a href="/wiki/Shanghai_Electric" title="Shanghai Electric">Shanghai Electric</a>-Alstom/<a href="/wiki/Nanjing_Puzhen_Rolling_Stock_Works" title="Nanjing Puzhen Rolling Stock Works">Nanjing Puzhen Rolling Stock Co., Ltd.</a> six car sets – Line 10</li>
<li>24 Nanjing Puzhen Rolling Stock Works six car sets - Line 13</li>
<li>46 Siemens &amp; CSR Zhuzhou three car sets - Two sets are coupled to form a six car train.</li>
</ul>
<p>Most lines currently use 6 car sets, with the exceptions being:</p>
<ul>
<li>Lines 5, 6, and a section of line 2 which use 4 car sets.</li>
<li>Some trains on line 8 use 7 car sets.</li>
<li>Line 1 and line 2 use 8 car sets.</li>
</ul>
<h3><span class="mw-headline" id="Signalling">Signalling</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Shanghai_Metro&amp;action=edit&amp;section=21" title="Edit section: Signalling">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h3>
<p>Shanghai Metro lines 6, 7, 8, 9, 10 and 11 are equipped with <a href="/wiki/Communications-based_train_control" title="Communications-based train control">CBTC</a> systems capable of headways as low as 90 seconds.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-69"><a href="#cite_note-69">[67]</a></sup></p>
<h3><span class="mw-headline" id="Power_supply">Power supply</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Shanghai_Metro&amp;action=edit&amp;section=22" title="Edit section: Power supply">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h3>
<p>In contrast to many other metro systems in the world, the Shanghai Metro uses <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Overhead_lines" title="Overhead lines">overhead wires</a> for the power supply, except for Line 16 which uses <a href="/wiki/Third_rail" title="Third rail">third rail</a>.</p>
<p>On Line 2, Siemens Transportation Systems equipped the line with an overhead contact line (cantilever material: galvanized steel) and 7 DC traction power supply substations.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-70"><a href="#cite_note-70">[68]</a></sup></p>
<h3><span class="mw-headline" id="Passenger_information_systems">Passenger information systems</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Shanghai_Metro&amp;action=edit&amp;section=23" title="Edit section: Passenger information systems">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h3>
<p>Plasma screens on the platforms show passengers when the next two trains are coming, along with advertisements and public service announcements. The subway cars contain <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Liquid_crystal_display" title="Liquid crystal display">LCD</a> screens showing advertisements and on some lines, the next stop, while above-ground trains have <a href="/wiki/Light-emitting_diode" title="Light-emitting diode">LED</a> screens showing the next stop. The LED screens are being phased in on Line 1 and are also included in lines 7 and 9, two underground lines. There are recorded messages stating the next stop in Mandarin, English and (on line 16 only) <a href="/wiki/Shanghainese" title="Shanghainese">Shanghainese</a>,<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-sh.sina.com.cn_67-1"><a href="#cite_note-sh.sina.com.cn-67">[65]</a></sup><sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-71"><a href="#cite_note-71">[69]</a></sup> but the messages stating nearby attractions or shops for a given station (a form of paid advertising) are in Mandarin only. The metro operating company is resistant to expanding use of <a href="/wiki/Shanghainese" title="Shanghainese">Shanghainese</a> for announcing stops, on the basis that, on most lines, the majority of passengers can understand either Mandarin or English.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-72"><a href="#cite_note-72">[70]</a></sup></p>
<p>Station signs are in Chinese and English. The Metro authority is testing a new systematic numbering system for stations on <a href="/wiki/Line_10,_Shanghai_Metro" title="Line 10, Shanghai Metro">Line 10</a>.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-73"><a href="#cite_note-73">[71]</a></sup></p>
<h2><span class="mw-headline" id="Future_expansion">Future expansion</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Shanghai_Metro&amp;action=edit&amp;section=24" title="Edit section: Future expansion">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h2>
<p>The Shanghai Metro system is one of the fastest growing metro systems in the world. Four lines were under construction at the end of 2014, and nine other lines or sections began construction in 2015. By the end of 2020, the network will comprise 18 lines spanning 800 kilometres (497 mi).<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-plan201412_74-0"><a href="#cite_note-plan201412-74">[72]</a></sup> In addition, there are long-term plans to connect the Shanghai Metro with the <a href="/wiki/Suzhou_Rail_Transit" title="Suzhou Rail Transit">Suzhou Rail Transit</a> and <a href="/wiki/Wuxi_Metro" title="Wuxi Metro">Wuxi Metro</a> in neighbouring <a href="/wiki/Jiangsu" title="Jiangsu">Jiangsu</a> province.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-suzhouwuxi_13-1"><a href="#cite_note-suzhouwuxi-13">[11]</a></sup></p>

<td>Airport Line</td>
<td></td>
<td><a href="/wiki/Pudong_International_Airport_Station" title="Pudong International Airport Station">Pudong International Airport</a></td>
<td><a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Hongqiao_Railway_Station" title="Hongqiao Railway Station">Hongqiao Railway Station</a></td>
<td>68</td>
<td>8</td>
<td>Planned</td>
</tr>
</table>
<h2><span class="mw-headline" id="Incidents">Incidents</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Shanghai_Metro&amp;action=edit&amp;section=25" title="Edit section: Incidents">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h2>
<ul>
<li>December 22, 2009—at about 5:50 am, an electrical fault in the tunnel between <a href="/wiki/South_Shaanxi_Road_Station" title="South Shaanxi Road Station">South Shaanxi Road Station</a> and <a href="/wiki/People%27s_Square_Station" title="People's Square Station">People's Square Station</a> caused a few trains to stall. While the track was under repair, a low-speed collision occurred between two trains on Line 1, trapping scores of passengers underground for up to two hours and affecting millions of early commuters. Nobody was injured, but the front of the train was badly damaged. Service resumed at around 12:15 pm.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-77"><a href="#cite_note-77">[75]</a></sup><sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-78"><a href="#cite_note-78">[76]</a></sup></li>
<li>July 5, 2010—at the <a href="/wiki/Zhongshan_Park_Station" title="Zhongshan Park Station">Zhongshan Park Station</a> a woman died after trying to crowd into a subway train as the doors were closing. With her wrist trapped in the train doors, she was dragged between the train and the <a href="/wiki/Platform_screen_doors" title="Platform screen doors">platform screen doors</a> when the train started moving.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-79"><a href="#cite_note-79">[77]</a></sup></li>
<li>September 27, 2011—at 2:51 pm, two trains on Line 10 collided between <a href="/wiki/Yuyuan_Garden_Station" title="Yuyuan Garden Station">Yuyuan Garden Station</a> and <a href="/wiki/Laoximen_Station" title="Laoximen Station">Laoximen Station</a>, injuring 284 - 300 people. Initial investigations found that train operators violated regulations while operating the trains manually after a loss of power on the line caused its signal system to fail. No deaths were reported.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-80"><a href="#cite_note-80">[78]</a></sup></li>
</ul>

<h2><span class="mw-headline" id="Notes">Notes</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Shanghai_Metro&amp;action=edit&amp;section=27" title="Edit section: Notes">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h2>
<div class="reflist" style="list-style-type: decimal;">
<ol class="references">
<li id="cite_note-exclude-maglev-22-1"><span class="mw-cite-backlink">^ <a href="#cite_ref-exclude-maglev-22_1-0"><sup><i><b>a</b></i></sup></a> <a href="#cite_ref-exclude-maglev-22_1-1"><sup><i><b>b</b></i></sup></a> <a href="#cite_ref-exclude-maglev-22_1-2"><sup><i><b>c</b></i></sup></a> <a href="#cite_ref-exclude-maglev-22_1-3"><sup><i><b>d</b></i></sup></a> <a href="#cite_ref-exclude-maglev-22_1-4"><sup><i><b>e</b></i></sup></a></span> <span class="reference-text">This figure excludes <a href="/wiki/Shanghai_Maglev_Train" title="Shanghai Maglev Train">Maglev line</a> and <a href="/wiki/Line_22,_Shanghai_Metro" title="Line 22, Shanghai Metro">Line 22</a>, both often included in Shanghai Metro maps but not considered part of the system.</span></li>
<li id="cite_note-Stncount-2"><span class="mw-cite-backlink">^ <a href="#cite_ref-Stncount_2-0"><sup><i><b>a</b></i></sup></a> <a href="#cite_ref-Stncount_2-1"><sup><i><b>b</b></i></sup></a> <a href="#cite_ref-Stncount_2-2"><sup><i><b>c</b></i></sup></a></span> <span class="reference-text">337 is the number of stations if interchanges on different lines are counted separately, with the exception of the 9 stations shared by Lines 3 and 4 on the same track. The stations on the <a href="/wiki/Shanghai_Maglev_Train" title="Shanghai Maglev Train">Maglev line</a> and <a href="/wiki/Jinshan_Railway" title="Jinshan Railway">Line 22</a> are not included.</span></li>
</ol>
</div>
